<div id="review_1446836131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446836131" />
    <a title="Ten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42637439-ten"><img alt="Ten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436918503p2/42637439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446836131?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ten" href="/user/show/42637439-ten">Ten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142409411" href="/book/show/499118.The_Looking_Glass_Wars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42637439-ten?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42637439-ten?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42637439-ten?shelf=parallel-universes">parallel-universes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42637439-ten?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446836131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10781303777325477253"><i> Also on <a href='http://inherentlybookish.blogspot.com/2015/11/review-looking-glass-wars.html' rel='nofollow noopener'> Inherently Bookish </a> </i><br/><br/>I am saddened to say that this is my first 1-star rating in 2015. I was doing so well, reading books that weren't always perfect, and yet I always found something in them I could enjoy. And then my roommate recommended this book to me, and I found myself taking it. It seemed interesting: a completely new take on Alice In Wonderland, one in which Alice does not stumble blindly down a rabbit hole, but in which she is a princess of Wonderland, brought to Earth as a mea</span>
  <span id="freeText10781303777325477253" style="display:none"><i> Also on <a href="http://inherentlybookish.blogspot.com/2015/11/review-looking-glass-wars.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Inherently Bookish </a> </i><br /><br />I am saddened to say that this is my first 1-star rating in 2015. I was doing so well, reading books that weren't always perfect, and yet I always found something in them I could enjoy. And then my roommate recommended this book to me, and I found myself taking it. It seemed interesting: a completely new take on Alice In Wonderland, one in which Alice does not stumble blindly down a rabbit hole, but in which she is a princess of Wonderland, brought to Earth as a means of protection when her family is murdered by her evil Aunt Redd.<br /><br />It could have been amazing. But was it?<br /><br />No.<br /><br />This was not a bad book. And yet, after finishing it, I couldn't name one thing about it in which I enjoyed. <br /><br />While the premise may have been intriguing, the execution was not handled well.<br /><br />The author tried to create something completely new, while also trying to keep the main characters that were so beloved in Alice in Wonderland. Unfortunately, he did not succeed. Most of the ways he twisted these characters made me raise my eyebrows, like the White Rabbit being a man with rather large ears named Bibwit Harte and Alice being named Alyss. I couldn't understand the author's decision to change the spelling of her name, other than it being a "clever ploy" to get the reader's attention. All of these changes seemed pointless and did not work for me.<br /><br />The pacing itself was off, and I couldn't quite get a grip on the story. The novel itself spans at least fourteen years, from Alyss as a young girl at age 7, and continuing on until she was over the age of twenty. This is a very broad span of time for a novel to cover, and the author did not manage it well. It seemed choppy, with parts seeming to skim by without the reader having enough time to grasp the events that happened.<br /><br />The storyline tried to be something different, and it was. But it just did not intrigue me. I found myself skimming pages, waiting for it to be over. I found a lot of the dialogue stinted, lacking a sense of realism that really hurt my enjoyment of the novel.<br /><br />The only thing that caught my attention was the use of imagination as a sort of "superpower." Imagination in this novel was a tangible thing, in which the user could create anything they willed. Although intriguing, it wasn't explained enough, and it also seemed like a means for the main characters to do whatever they wanted with little to no challenge. Alyss loses her imagination when she leaves Wonderland, and yet she seems to get it back almost immediately after returning, and is soon more powerful than anyone else, despite only practicing a few limited times.<br /><br />Overall, there was so much potential, but it just wasn't executed well. I will not be continuing with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10781303777325477253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123910082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123910082" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123910082?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405219761" href="/book/show/289740.The_Looking_Glass_Wars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=retellings-continuations">retellings-continuations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=unfinished-2011">unfinished-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123910082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15465802922099729795">The Looking Glass Wars is not really different from what I had expected. It is a well-constructed retelling, that places Alice as the Queen of Hearts' daughter and consequently the next-in-line for Wonderland's throne. When the evil Red Queen, Queen Genevieve's sister, attacks the palace with her army of card soldiers, Alice - or Alyss - is sent via the Pool of Tears tunnel to a parallel world - ours, but during the life-time of Lewis Carroll, by the Queen's faithful bodyguard Hatter Madigan (yo</span>
  <span id="freeText15465802922099729795" style="display:none">The Looking Glass Wars is not really different from what I had expected. It is a well-constructed retelling, that places Alice as the Queen of Hearts' daughter and consequently the next-in-line for Wonderland's throne. When the evil Red Queen, Queen Genevieve's sister, attacks the palace with her army of card soldiers, Alice - or Alyss - is sent via the Pool of Tears tunnel to a parallel world - ours, but during the life-time of Lewis Carroll, by the Queen's faithful bodyguard Hatter Madigan (you know him), to keep her safe until things have calmed down. Is <i>is</i> kind of fun recognizing the elements of the well-known story and noticing how cleverly they are twisted. But nonetheless I feel inexplicably bored. Why I cannot say. A second sore spot is Alyss age and her behavior during the first chapters. Yes, even I dreamed of certain boys in kindergarden, and yes, I know, princesses start thinking about marriages and political alliances quite early, but that dancing-almost-kissing scene between seven year old Alyss and her ten year old devoted commoner friend Dodge of the royal guard and their respective hidden feelings for each other was depicted far too mature and lovey-dovey in an unrealistic sort of way to me. Add ten years each and it's alright. My opinion is that if an author cannot even partly remember what it was like to be seven should avoid shoving the spotlight on a character of that particular age.<br /><br />So, I decided to let the book drop at page 80. This is not meant as an discouragement to pick it up and try. Heads-off-screaming Queen Redd is fun and the Diamond Prince's deflated bottom a nice thing to visualize.<br /><br />Tina, please assign another book to me. I am ready to switch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15465802922099729795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1019899522860038225" style="display:none"><b>Book: The Looking Glass Wars (The Looking Glass Wars, #1) <br />Author: Frank Beddor<br />Awesomeness level: 5/5<br />Began: November 9, 2009<br />Finished: November 14, 2009</b><br /><br />It was a long time ago when I saw <i>Seeing Redd</i>, Frank Beddor's second book in The Looking Glass Wars trilogy, at Barnes &amp; Noble. I didn't know I'd squeal with excitment when Hatter Madigan or any other characters supporting White Imagination were mentioned.<br />In short, I didn't know how amazing this book would be.<br /><br />Alyss Heart is seven years old when the fantastic story begins, and separated from her parents when her murderous aunt Redd attacks the Heart Palace, wanting the crown for herself. Alyss and her bodygaurd, Hatter Madigan, escape on the Queen's orders to the Pool of Tears. Where does it lead? No one knows, for the simple reason that no one's ever returned.<br />Where does it lead?<br />The Pool of Tears leads to a very strange world--<i>Our own.</i><br />Alyss and Hatter are separated, Alyss turns up in Victorian London, Hatter in Paris. <br />Hatter spends 13 years searching the world for her, detirmined to find her so they can return to Wonderland and battle Redd for her rightful place as the Queen of Hearts.<br />Alyss, meanwhile, is told her stories of Wonderland are rubbish, but she knows better...Right?<br />Will Hatter and Alyss find each other, and can she succed in battling her evil aunt Redd?<br /></span>

<div id="review_1923494433" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923494433" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923494433?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Alice in Wonderland fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=famous-literary-historical-characte">famous-literary-historical-characte</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=the-lost-heir">the-lost-heir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=alice-in-wonderland">alice-in-wonderland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=alternate-dimension-or-world">alternate-dimension-or-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923494433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15759199750963933015">Somewhere along the way I became obsessed with Alice in Wonderland. Not quite sure when and why. Well, I think it's the weirdness and the color of the world. The darkness is there, but this book definitely brings it to the forefront. I am continually looking for more stories built on the Alice in Wonderland concept. This really fits the bill.<br/><br/>What if there truly was a war between the Red Queen and the White Queens? What if being queen endowed the ruler with unfathomable powers of imagination that</span>
  <span id="freeText15759199750963933015" style="display:none">Somewhere along the way I became obsessed with Alice in Wonderland. Not quite sure when and why. Well, I think it's the weirdness and the color of the world. The darkness is there, but this book definitely brings it to the forefront. I am continually looking for more stories built on the Alice in Wonderland concept. This really fits the bill.<br /><br />What if there truly was a war between the Red Queen and the White Queens? What if being queen endowed the ruler with unfathomable powers of imagination that can be used for good or bad? What if two sisters became mortal enemies, even to the degree that one would plot and execute a bloody takeover? That's the plot of this book.<br /><br />I liked how Alice in Wonderland is treated as a real story that was wrongly interpreted. Alyss is taken by her bodyguard (when Wonderland falls to Queen Redd's assault) to Victorian England through a magical fountain to save her life. She's separated from her bodyguard and has to fend for herself in England. Initially she has her power of imagination but it fades the longer she is away from Wonderland. She ends up getting adopted by a vicar's family and goes under the name of Alice Liddell (the girl to whom Lewis Carroll first told his Alice in Wonderland story). She tells her story to another young vicar who plagarizes and changes some information. For instance, Alyss's name was spelled wrong. Alyss's bodyguard is Hatter Madigan, sort of what would happen if the Mad Hatter was a ninja and used his hat as a glaive spinning weapon. That part was really cool. I liked Alyss. She's young and strong-willed, and grows a lot over the course of this book. She was a bit spoiled at first, but tremendous loss shapes her into a young woman who will be an excellent ruler. <br /><br />This is a dark and bloody read. Queen Redd is irredeemably evil. She wreaks a lot havoc due to her corrupt, hate-filled heart and need for revenge and constant adulation. She has no qualms about murdering her family, including her young niece. She makes a lot of people miserable, even when she doesn't kill them.<br /><br />I liked how Beddor takes the story of Alice and Wonderland and creates his own series around it. Most of the elements are there, but with nice twists. The romance aspect is new to this story, but it was likeable, as well as the character of Dodge Anders, who is Alyss' love interest. The Cheshire Cat becomes a genetically modified assassin with nine lives who claims more than a few lives. The White Rabbit is a learned adviser to the Queen. The playing card army is divides into two factions, one loyal to the original queen and become freedom fighters in Alyss's name, and the genetically modified and degenerate creation of Queen Redd's black imaginations. <br /><br />This is a good book for tweens and teens who like this sort of fantasy. It's too scary and bloody for younger readers. It has a lot of good action sequences and that magic of Wonderland is exquisitely illustrated through the narrative. I enjoyed listening to it, and I will pick up the next volumes on audiobook as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15759199750963933015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The book makes it a world of imagination, which even inspires the imaginary of all other worlds—and it just…fits. <div id="review_907152536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907152536" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907152536?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=it-is-okay">it-is-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907152536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1057689398956874095">It's an imaginative retelling of Alice In Wonderland, it's somewhere between 3 stars to 3.5 stars. I <i>love</i> the world building, the action scenes are nice and the plots keep me entertaining for the whole time. But I found almost all of the characters have no development and it's quite boring for the good guys to be always good and the villains to have no other purpose nor personality outside of being power-crazed, sadistic and well, just plain evil. Plus the Good vs. Evil theme is a bit too simple</span>
  <span id="freeText1057689398956874095" style="display:none">It's an imaginative retelling of Alice In Wonderland, it's somewhere between 3 stars to 3.5 stars. I <i>love</i> the world building, the action scenes are nice and the plots keep me entertaining for the whole time. But I found almost all of the characters have no development and it's quite boring for the good guys to be always good and the villains to have no other purpose nor personality outside of being power-crazed, sadistic and well, just plain evil. Plus the Good vs. Evil theme is a bit too simple-minded to my liking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1057689398956874095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_960476863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/960476863" />
    <a title="Yomna hosny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9096571-yomna-hosny"><img alt="Yomna hosny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549992988p2/9096571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/960476863?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yomna hosny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yomna hosny" href="/user/show/9096571-yomna-hosny">Yomna hosny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142409411" href="/book/show/499118.The_Looking_Glass_Wars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096571-yomna-hosny?shelf=i-own-a-copy">i-own-a-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960476863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer486080675526047087">This is one of those book that people either love with the fiery vengeance of a thousand suns or loathe so completely they wish eternal doom and damnation onto everyone who so much as hints that they liked it.<br/><br/>I gave it a firm five stars so.. :D<br/><br/>Original review can be found here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://theliteraryinsomniac.tumblr.com/post/88523689504/the-looking-glass-wars-the-looking-glass-wars-book'>http://theliteraryinsomniac.tumblr.co...</a><br/><br/>Anyways.. allow me to explain myself. Ahem.<br/><br/><br/><br/>This book uses actual historical events to create parallel, similar events in the story. elements from the second world war, The american </span>
  <span id="freeText486080675526047087" style="display:none">This is one of those book that people either love with the fiery vengeance of a thousand suns or loathe so completely they wish eternal doom and damnation onto everyone who so much as hints that they liked it.<br /><br />I gave it a firm five stars so.. :D<br /><br />Original review can be found here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://theliteraryinsomniac.tumblr.com/post/88523689504/the-looking-glass-wars-the-looking-glass-wars-book">http://theliteraryinsomniac.tumblr.co...</a><br /><br />Anyways.. allow me to explain myself. Ahem.<br /><br /><br /><br />This book uses actual historical events to create parallel, similar events in the story. elements from the second world war, The american civil war and several other key moments in history are incorporated. I hadn’t realized that at first. but when I read the timeline at the end of the book, I was really blown away by the depth of detail that went into this.<br /><br />This book, aside from being a beautifully designed book with 8 pages of full color, glossy inserts of art showing gorgeous renditions of the main characters, several dividers and margin art on every page, is a “big” story. <br /><br />it covers a significant portion of a country’s history in leaps and bounds. events happen and you get to see their far off consequences a few pages later. And it manages to keep that pace throughout the entire book.<br /><br />This might be an Alice in wonderland re-imagining but it’s wholly unique. It combines fantasy and magic with futuristic, science-y technology for an incredibly entertaining effect. but at its heart, it’s a story about the triumph of good over evil and loyalty and a coming of age story and a story about lost love and how people who change never really become the same ever again.<br /><br />Alyss Heart is the future queen of wonderland. A child, still when her mother, Queesn genevive is killed and overthrown by REDD, genevive’s sister.<br /><br />The main conflict between the two sisters is Redd’s use of her magical, imaginative abilities in the service of evil, selfish whims and Genevive, being the “good guy” becoming favored by her parents so much that Redd is denied the right to the throne to which she is rightfully entitled by right of succession. (she’s the eldest of the two sisters)<br /><br />Ensue revenge and plotting, war and plunder. In the middle of all that is little seven year old Alyss who gets cut off from her home and forced to suppress her roots in the human world. Only finding comfort when a man approaches her to tell her story in a book. a book that he changes, twists and defiles so much that is a gross bastardization of the true story that Alyss told. The man even spells her name wrong. Alice.<br /><br />This book is going straight into my 214 favorites pile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="486080675526047087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wFBIgdrownNEKSbBS3a9u7dec1wZD/FLjdSvbu8nhNFrMhmuhV9JrpHXYaefXfVPe09NAcmxMkWD9/IrToODRw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gRtFyPgYLyFskYlVH5VnmPY4v5z0EF8zJylNlIwRXMgqeRTnp6+k/LlvzjPLvi9sOimBwSSunD0pChDRLbVbXg==')})
  }

Le but de cette école que l’on intègre sur concours après deux années d’université au minimum est de former l’élite journalistique puisque le centre, situé à Paris rue du Louvre, se targue lui-même d’être &quot;une école d’excellence&quot;. En fait d’excellence, François Ruffin, qui est sorti de l’école il y a peu, a surtout trouvé une gigantesque machine qui &quot;fabrique des journalistes-techniciens à même de produire une information-marchandise qui alimente l’industrie de la presse&quot;. Rassemblant quantité de souvenirs personnels, de paroles d’étudiants qui ont connu le même désenchantement, citant la parole des directeurs exhortant cette petite troupe d’élites à ne pas réfléchir, François Ruffin raconte de l’intérieur comment on devient &quot;un gratte-papier obéissant&quot;, &quot;habitué à produire du vide&quot;. L’habitude de recopier les dépêches AFP, la logique de remplissage, la collusion trop fréquente entre information et communication (le plus souvent au profit de grandes firmes), la reproduction des poncifs et clichés et, en conséquence, la négation de tout style et de toute pensée, l’acceptation &quot;d’un mode de production routinier&quot;, et surtout la connivence entre tous le médias, prédisposés à faire plus ou moins tous la même chose… Ruffin met en scène le théâtre (de marionnettes) du journalisme tel qu’il le conçoit. \nLes Petits Soldats du journalisme ne se veut pas un pamphlet. Pas non plus, malgré les apparences, une dénonciation virulente. Il s’agit d’une enquête sans concession menée par un ancien élève de l’école qui s’insurge contre l’appauvrissement du contenu des médias. Voilà qui permettra aux lecteurs non compatissants de prendre la distance qui leur conviendra... Le texte de François Ruffin est accompagné de plusieurs dessins humoristiques et satiriques de Faujour. L’un deux représente un directeur de l’information sermonnant son stagiaire : &quot;On s’en fout que tu n’aies rien à dire, l’important c’est de l’écrire&quot;… --Denis Gombert \n\n\n\nPrésentation de l\'éditeur\n\nLe Centre de formation des journalistes se proclame &quot; la meilleure école de journalisme en France et même en Europe &quot;. Patrick Poivre d\'Arvor, David Pujadas, Pierre Lescure, Franz-Olivier Giesbert, Laurent Joffrin et tant d\'autres ténors de la presse sont passés dans ses murs.\nPendant deux ans, François Ruffin a suivi leur exemple. Elève appliqué, il a pris en notes les conseils des professeurs et les confidences des &quot; grandes plumes &quot;. Il s\'est coulé dans le moule, pour voir. Et il a vu.\n&quot; Dans un an, vous serez journalistes, confie un intervenant. Vous entrerez dans ce que j\'appelle &quot; le complot de famille &quot;, c\'est-à-dire des règles qui peuvent scandaliser les gens mais, bon, c\'est comme ça que la machine fonctionne. &quot; Un &quot; complot &quot; que ce livre met au jour : tacites ailleurs, les règles du métier sont ici affichées sans vergogne.\nComme dans un miroir grossissant, le journalisme ordinaire se révèle alors sans fard : la célébration du vide, le mépris du public, la soumission aux pouvoirs, la quête du profit, l\'information prémâchée comme seul horizon...\nUn récit incisif et insolent qui démonte, pièce à pièce, les rouages de la machine médiatique.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3215427011815837979\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17980111046740486997">Literary Sleuth and world creator Frank Beddor dared to expose the true story of Wonderland in the New York Times bestselling young adult trilogy The Looking Glass Wars. To satisfy the awakened curiosity of his readers he continued to tell the parallel adventures of Royal Bodyguard Hatter Madigan’s search for the lost princess in the graphic novel series Hatter M. He lives in Los Angeles.</span>
